## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating an ordinary differential equation (ODE) for population dynamics. With only (t, P) available, common structures include per-capita growth depending on density (P), environmental forcing over time (t), and terms representing mortality, competition, or harvesting.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant net flux (immigration/emigration): dP_dt = c0 (net inflow/outflow independent of P)
- Linear density-dependent per-capita rate: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P) (competition/self-limitation via quadratic term)
- Higher-order crowding: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2) (multi-body interference or strong density dependence)
- Power-law growth/decay: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric or phenomenological scaling of net growth with population)
- Gompertz growth (continuous): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (crowding acts through logarithmic decline of per-capita growth)
- Generalized theta-logistic form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence; c2 tunes approach to carrying capacity)
- Richards-type generalized growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (additional shape control for sigmoidal growth in P)
- Strong Allee effect with upper limit: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (negative growth below threshold c1; decline above c2)
- Weak Allee effect (per-capita boost at low density): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 / (P + c2)) * (1 - c3 * P) (enhanced growth at small P with eventual crowding)
- Constant harvesting/stock removal: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (proportional growth minus fixed quota harvest)
- Density-dependent mortality/harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (loss increases superlinearly with crowding or effort)
- Seasonal forcing of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Secular environmental trend in growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying per-capita rate due to warming/resources/technology trend)
- Transient perturbation (pulse event): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * exp(-c2 * (t - c3)**2) (short-lived shock independent of P, e.g., release/stocking)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Work with per-capita growth g(t,P) = dP_dt / P: if g decreases with P, it indicates density dependence (crowding/competition).
- Quadratic or higher powers in P inside dP_dt (e.g., +c*P**2, +c*P**3) typically represent interaction-driven effects such as competition or aggregation processes.
- A log term log(c/P) in dP_dt is characteristic of Gompertz-type regulation, where relative growth decays roughly linearly with log(P).
- Factors like (P - cA) in dP_dt encode Allee thresholds: growth becomes negative for P < cA (mate limitation/cooperation failure).
- Additive constants in dP_dt (Â±c0) suggest external forcing independent of population size, such as constant immigration, emigration, or constant quota harvest.
- Sin(c*t + phase) or cos(c*t + phase) modulating P indicates seasonality (periodic resources, breeding seasons), often producing oscillations around a trend.
- Explicit exp(c*t) multipliers indicate nonstationary environments: accelerating/declining carrying conditions over time rather than purely density-driven regulation.
- Terms combining t and P (e.g., P*(c0 + c1*t)) suggest a time-varying per-capita growth rate (changing habitat quality or management).
- Superlinear loss terms (e.g., -c*P**c1 with c1>1) imply mortality/harvest pressure increases disproportionately with density, which can create sharp collapses.

Key structural properties of GT:
- Depends on **both** \(P\) and \(t\).
- \(t\)-dependence is **exactly** \(aP e^{-kt}\): multiplicative in \(P\) and an exponential in \(t\).

**Candidate 30:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*Abs(P + c7) + 1) + c8)`
- Has `P*exp(c2*t)` â€” this matches the form `P*exp(-b*t)` with c2 = -b. 
- Also has `P*c0` (linear in P).
- Has `sin(c5*log(c6*|P+c7|+1))` â€” this is a sin(log(...)) type function.
- GT has `P*exp(-b*P)` term. Can sin(log(...)) match `P*exp(-b*P)`?

Let me check: GT = `a*P - a*P*exp(-b*P) + a*P*exp(-b*t)`

Candidate 30 = `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|P+c7|+1) + c8)`

The `P*c1*exp(c2*t)` can match `a*P*exp(-b*t)` with c1=a, c2=-b.
The `P*c0` can match `a*P` with c0=a.
We need `c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|P+c7|+1) + c8) + c3` to match `-a*P*exp(-b*P)`.

But `-a*P*exp(-b*P)` is not a sin(log(...)) function. These are fundamentally different. sin(log(...)) oscillates; P*exp(-bP) doesn't oscillate. Cannot match.

Candidate 30 verdict: [NO MATCH]
